20/06/2022, 1:14 pm - Fahad Shaikh: For some students who had asked..
How-to-disable-login-password in Ubuntu:

Open the terminal

sudo visudo

Find the line that says:
%admin ALL=(ALL) ALL

And change it to:
%admin ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD: ALL

Save and exit the file.
https://askubuntu.com/questions/354216/how-to-disable-login-password

For adding user in ubuntu:
sudo adduser username
https://linuxize.com/post/how-to-add-and-delete-users-on-ubuntu-20-04/

08/07/2022, 12:30 pm - +92 312 4305033: *Uptime Command in Linux*
It is used to find out how long the system is active (running). This command returns set of values that involve, the current time, and the amount of time system is in running state, number of users currently logged into, and the load time for the past 1, 5 and 15 minutes respectively.
*Syntax:*
uptime [-options]
*Example:*
abdulmajeed@Delta1$ uptime
22:20:33 up 620 days, 22:37, 1 user, load average: 0.03, 0.10, 0.10
‚Ä¢	22:20:33 - The current system time.
‚Ä¢	up 620 days, 22:37 - The length of time the system has been up.
‚Ä¢	1 user - The number of logged-in users.
‚Ä¢	load average: 0.03, 0.10, 0.10 - System load averages for the past 1, 5, and 15 minutes.
*Options:*
 -p, --pretty   show uptime in pretty format
 -h, --help     display this help and exit
 -s, --since    system up since
 -V, --version output version information and exit

08/07/2022, 5:42 pm - +92 312 4305033: *Uname Command in Linux*
Uname is a Linux command-line utility that displays basic system information. It prints operating system details and machine hardware platform information of your Linux computer
*Syntax:*
uname [OPTIONS]...
*The options are as follows:*
Option	Description
-a	Display all information about the operating system, Kernel version, and hardware
-n	Display only the network node hostname [--nodename]
-s	Display the Kernel name
-r	Display the Kernel release version [--kernel-name]
-v	Display the Kernel version with date
-m	Display the hardware platform name of the system
-p	Display the processor type
-o	Display the operating system name
--help	Display help and exit

*Example:*
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname -n
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname -v
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname -nrvmpio
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname -a
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname -s -n
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ uname ‚Äìhelp

09/07/2022, 12:32 am - +92 312 4305033: *ls [List] Command*
is generally used to list files and directories in the file system.  Just like File explorer for GUI, ls command is a CLI version.
*Syntax:*
	ls [options] [file-name/directory-name]
*Options:*
‚Ä¢	ls -a lists hidden files along with other files and directories.
‚Ä¢	ls -al lists files and directories with file permissions, ownership, and etc.
‚Ä¢	ls -r Sort contents in the reverse order
‚Ä¢	ls -t Sort by time, newest at top
‚Ä¢	ls -R List Subdirectories Recursively
‚Ä¢	ls -X Display alphabetically by file extension
‚Ä¢	ls . to list files and directories in the current directory
‚Ä¢	ls .. to list files and directories in the parent directory
‚Ä¢	ls -lh long listing format of files and directories
‚Ä¢	ls -d */ to list only directories
‚Ä¢	ls -l | egrep -v '^d' To list only files
‚Ä¢	ls >filename  to redirect the output in a text file.
‚Ä¢	*  This wildcard is used to represent any character, or even no characters at all	
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls -al
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls ./..	up one level
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls ./../.. 	up two level	
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls >fileslist.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat fileslist.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls cnc 	to show files in cnc directory	
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls *.txt	to show all txt files
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ ls m*. *	to show all files start with m

clear is a standard Unix computer operating system command that is used to clear the terminal screen.  In order to clear the terminal press [ctrl+l]
*Syntax:*
	clear
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ clear
*Cat command*
cat (short for ‚Äúconcatenate ‚Äú) command allows us to create single or multiple files, view content of a file, concatenate files and redirect output in terminal or files.
*Syntax:*
	cat [options] filename(s)
*Options:*
‚Ä¢	-n to display the line number of file content.
‚Ä¢	>filename   creating a file with the specified name and press CTL+d to save content
‚Ä¢	|more or |less   to view file content with scroll.
‚Ä¢	>>filename   to append content in specified file
‚Ä¢	*   use wildcard to view content of all files
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat fileslist.txt to display content of file
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat file1.txt file2.txt to display content of both files
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat file1.txt >file3.txt copy file1 content to file3
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat file1.txt file3.txt >file4.txt copy both file content to file4
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat -n file4.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat >test.txt input content into file & then ‚ÄòCtrl+d‚Äô to save file.
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat test.txt |more
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat file1.txt >>file3.txt to append file1content to file3
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat file1.txt file2.txt >>file3.txt append both file content in file3
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat * to view content of all files
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cat *.txt to view content of all text files
*pwd command*
pwd stands for Print Working Directory. It prints the path of the working directory, starting from the root.
*Syntax:*
	pwd [-options]
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ pwd

09/07/2022, 6:18 pm - +92 312 4305033: *mkdir command*
mkdir (make directory) command in Linux allows the user to create directories (also referred to as folders in some operating systems). This command can create multiple directories at once 
*Syntax:*
	mkdir [options...] [directories ...]
*Options:*
‚Ä¢	-p  to create parent directories as necessary.
‚Ä¢	-m a=rwx  to set the file modes.R for read(1), W for write(2) and X for execute(4)
‚Ä¢	{dirname1, dirname2...} to create multiple directories at once.
‚Ä¢	‚Äòdirectory name‚Äô  to create directory with white space..
*Example:*
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir cn
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir -p first/second/third
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir -m a=rwx test1
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir -m a=rrr test2
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir -m777 test3
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir {G1, G2, G3, G4} to create 4 directories at once
		abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ mkdir ‚Äòmy course‚Äô
*cd command*
cd command in linux known as change directory command. It is used to change current working directory. 
*Syntax:*
	cd [directory]
*Option:*
‚Ä¢	/ to change directory to the root directory, The root directory is the first directory in your filesystem hierarchy  
‚Ä¢	 ~  used to change directory to the home directory. 
‚Ä¢	 ..  used to move to the parent directory of current directory
‚Ä¢	.  or - to current directory.
‚Ä¢	directoryname  to move specified directory.
‚Ä¢	‚Äòdirectory name‚Äô   used to navigate to a directory with white spaces
‚Ä¢	dirname && ls  to change to a new directory and list its content simultaneously.
*Example:*
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd /
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd ~
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd ..
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd ‚Äì
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd test1
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd test/test2/test3
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd ‚Äòmy course‚Äô
abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ cd test1 && ls
‚ÄÉ
*rmdir command*
remove empty directories
*Syntax:*
	rmdir [-option] directories name ‚Ä¶..
*Options:*
‚Ä¢	-p  to remove all directories if empty.
‚Ä¢	{dirname1, dirname2...} to remove multiple directories at once.
‚Ä¢	‚Äòdirectory name‚Äô  to remove directory with white space.
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rmdir test1
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rmdir -p test1/test2
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rmdir {test1, test2, test3}
	
*rm command*
rm stands for remove here. rm command is used to remove files

*Syntax:*
	rm [OPTION]... FILE...
*Options:*
‚Ä¢	-i  ask the user for confirmation before removing each file
‚Ä¢	filename to remove a specified file.
‚Ä¢	filename1 filename2... to remove multiple files at once.
‚Ä¢	-r  to remove directory (recursive).
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rm file1.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rm file1.txt file2.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rm -i file1.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rm -i file1.txt file2.txt file.txt
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ rm -r notes to remove all directories and files.

10/07/2022, 6:04 pm - +92 312 4305033: *Shell Scripting*
A shell provides an interface to connect with the system. When we use an operating system, we indirectly interact with the shell. While using a terminal every time on any Linux distribution system, we interact with the shell. The main function of the shell is to interpret or analyze Linux commands. A shell takes commands from the user and translates them into the kernel‚Äôs understandable form
*Shell Script 01:*
Shell Script to print Hello World on the console
*Program*

#! /bin/bash
echo "Hello World!!!"

*Output*

$ chmod 755 hello_world.sh
$ sh hello_world.sh
Hello World!!!

*Description:*
#!/bin/bash
This is known as shebang in Unix. Shebang is a collection of characters or letters that consist of a number sign and exclamation mark, that is (#!) at the beginning of a script. the main function of a shell is to interpret the UNIX commands given by the user. Some other example shebangs are:
#!/bin/sh 		 ‚Äî Execute the file using sh, the Bourne shell, or a compatible shell
#!/bin/csh 		 ‚Äî Execute the file using csh, the C shell, or a compatible shell
#!/usr/bin/perl -T 	 ‚Äî Execute using Perl with the option for taint checks
#!/usr/bin/php 	 ‚Äî Execute the file using the PHP command line interpreter
#!/usr/bin/python -O ‚Äî Execute using Python with optimizations to code
#!/usr/bin/ruby 	 ‚Äî Execute using Ruby
*echo command*
The echo command is one of the most commonly and widely used built-in commands for Linux bash and C shells, that typically used in a scripting language and batch files to display a line of text/string on standard output or a file.

*Description:*
*Using Shell Variables*
A variable is a character string to which we assign a value. The value assigned could be a number, text, filename, device, or any other type of data.A variable is nothing more than a pointer to the actual data. The shell enables you to create, assign, and delete variables.
*Variable Names*
The name of a variable can contain only letters (a to z or A to Z), numbers (0 to 9) or the underscore character (_).
*Defining Variables*
	variable name=variable value
*For example:*
	Name=‚Äù Abdul Majeed‚Äù
	Batch=36
*Accessing Values*
To access the value stored in a variable, prefix its name with the dollar sign ($)
*For example:*
	$Name
	$Batch

11/07/2022, 9:13 am - +92 312 4305033: *Shell Script 04:*
Shell Script to print Fibonacci series
*Program*
#! /bin/bash
echo "Enter the value of n"
read n
a=0
b=1
count=2
echo "Fibonacci series:"
echo $a
echo $b
while [ $count -le $n ]
do
     fib=`expr $a + $b`
     a=$b
     b=$fib
     echo $fib
     count=`expr $count + 1`
done

*Output*
$ chmod 755 fibonacci_series.sh
$ sh fibonacci_series.sh
Enter the value of n
6
Fibonacci series:
0
1
1
2
3
5
8

*Description:*
*Fibonacci series*
The Fibonacci sequence is a type series where each number is the sum of the two that precede it. It starts from 0 and 1 usually. The Fibonacci sequence is given by 0, 1, 1, 2, 3, 5, 8, 13, and so on. The numbers in the Fibonacci sequence are also called Fibonacci numbers. In Math, the sequence is defined as an ordered list of numbers that follow a specific pattern.
Fibonacci Sequence = 0, 1, 1, 2, 3, 5, 8, 13, ‚Ä¶.
‚Ä¢	‚Äú1‚Äù is obtained by adding the first and second term. (i.e., 0+1 = 1)
‚Ä¢	‚Äú2‚Äù is obtained by adding the second and third term (1+1 = 2)
‚Ä¢	‚Äú3‚Äù is obtained by adding the third and fourth term (1+2) and so on.
*Fibonacci Sequence Formula*
The Fibonacci sequence of numbers ‚ÄúFn‚Äù is defined using the recursive relation with the seed values F0=0 and F1=1:
Fn = Fn-1+Fn-2
*Fibonacci Sequence Solved Example*
Find the Fibonacci number when n=6, using recursive relation.
*Solution:*
The formula to calculate the Fibonacci Sequence is: Fn = Fn-1+Fn-2
Take: F0=0 and F1=1
Using the formula, we get
F2 = F1+F0 = 1+0 = 1
F3 = F2+F1 = 1+1 = 2
F4 = F3+F2 = 2+1 = 3
F5 = F4+F3 = 3+2 = 5
F6 = F5+F4 = 5+3 = 8
The *while loop* enables you to execute a set of commands repeatedly until some condition occurs. It is usually used when you need to manipulate the value of a variable repeatedly.
*Syntax:*
while [ condition]
           do
                 command1
                 command2
                 ..
                 ....
                 commandN
           done
*while loop Example*
Create a shell script called whileloop.sh:
#! /bin/bash
# set n to 1
n=1
# continue until $n less than 10
while [ $n -lt 10]
do
	echo "Welcome $n times."
	n=$(( n+1 ))	 # increments $n
done
*Save and close the file. Run it as follows:*
chmod 777 whileloop.sh
./whileloop.sh

The *expr command* in Linux evaluates a given expression and displays its corresponding output. expr is an external program used by Bourne shell. It uses expr external program with the help of backtick. The backtick (`) is actually called command substitution. It is used for:
‚Ä¢	Basic operations like addition, subtraction, multiplication, division, and modulus on integers.
‚Ä¢	Evaluating regular expressions, string operations like substring, length of strings etc.
*Syntax:*
	Variable=`expr expression`
*Example:*
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ echo ‚ÄúEnter two number in x and y‚Äù
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ read x
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ read y
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ sum=`expr $x+$y‚Äô
	abdulmajeed@Delta1~$ echo $sum
*Relational Operators*
Bourne Shell supports the following relational operators that are specific to numeric values. These operators do not work for string values unless their value is numeric.
*Operator	Description	Example*
-eq	Checks if the value of two operands are equal or not; if yes, then the condition becomes true.	[ $a -eq $b ] is not true.
-ne	Checks if the value of two operands are equal or not; if values are not equal, then the condition becomes true.	[ $a -ne $b ] is true.
-gt	Checks if the value of left operand is greater than the value of right operand; if yes, then the condition becomes true.	[ $a -gt $b ] is not true.
-lt	Checks if the value of left operand is less than the value of right operand; if yes, then the condition becomes true.	[ $a -lt $b ] is true.
-ge	Checks if the value of left operand is greater than or equal to the value of right operand; if yes, then the condition becomes true.	[ $a -ge $b ] is not true.
-le	Checks if the value of left operand is less than or equal to the value of right operand; if yes, then the condition becomes true.	[ $a -le $b ] is true.
11/07/2022, 9:15 am - +92 312 4305033: *Shell Script 05:*
Shell Script to find factorial of a number
*Program*
# !/bin/bash
echo "Enter a number"
read num
fact=1
n=$num;
while [ $num -ge 1 ]
do
	fact=`expr $fact \* $num`
	num=`expr $num - 1`
done
echo "Factorial of $n is $fact"
*Output*

$ sh factorial-of-number.sh 
Enter a number
7
Factorial of 7 is 5040

*Description:*
*Factorial*
Factorial of a whole number 'n' is defined as the product of that number with every whole number till 1. Symbolically, factorial can be represented as "!".
*Formula for n Factorial*
            n! =n√ó(n‚àí1)!
*For example:*
 the factorial of 4! is 4√ó3√ó2√ó1, which is equal to 24!

Shell Script to find biggest of two numbers
*Program*
#!/bin/sh
echo "Enter first number"
read a
echo "Enter second number"
read b

then
	echo $a "is greater"
else
	echo $b "is greater"

*Output*
$ chmod 755 biggest-of-two-numbers.sh
$ sh biggest-of-two-numbers.sh
Enter first number
98
Enter second number
12
98 is greater

*Description:*
The *if...elif...fi statement* is the one level advance form of control statement that allows Shell to make correct decision out of several conditions.
*Syntax*
if [ expression 1 ]
then
		Statement(s) to be executed if expression 1 is true
elif [ expression 2 ]
then
		Statement(s) to be executed if expression 2 is true
elif [ expression 3 ]
then
		Statement(s) to be executed if expression 3 is true
else
		Statement(s) to be executed if no expression is true
fi
*Example*
#!/bin/sh

a=10
b=20
echo ‚Äúvalue of a is:$a‚Äù
echo ‚Äúvalue of b is:$b‚Äù
if [ $a == $b ]
then
   echo "a is equal to b"
elif [ $a -gt $b ]
then
   echo "a is greater than b"
elif [ $a -lt $b ]
then
   echo "a is less than b"
else
   echo "None of the condition met"
fi

Shell Script to find biggest of three numbers using command line arguments
*Program*
#!/bin/bash
if [ $# -ne 3 ]
    then
	echo "$0: Numbers are not entered"
        exit 1
    fi
    
    n1=$1
    n2=$2
    n3=$3
    
    if [ $n1 -gt $n2 ] && [ $n1 -gt $n3 ]
    then
	echo "Number 1 is biggest: $n1"
    elif [ $n2 -gt $n1 ] && [ $n2 -gt $n3 ]
    then
	echo "Number 2 is biggest: $n2"
    elif [ $n3 -gt $n1 ] && [ $n3 -gt $n2 ]
    then
	echo "Number 3 is biggest: $n3"
    elif [ $1 -eq $2 ] && [ $1 -eq $3 ] && [ $2 -eq $3 ]
    then
	echo "All the three numbers are equal"
    else
        echo "Unable to determine"
    fi

*Output 1*
$ chmod 755 biggest-three-numbers-command-line.sh

Number 1 is biggest: 46

*Output 2*
$ sh biggest-three-numbers-command-line.sh 6 65 32
Number 2 is biggest: 65
*Output 3*
$ sh biggest-three-numbers-command-line.sh 6 12 39
Number 3 is biggest: 39

*Output 4*
$ sh biggest-three-numbers-command-line.sh 8 8 8
All the three numbers are equal

*Output 5*
$ sh biggest-three-numbers-command-line.sh 18 32 32
Unable to determine

*Description:*
*$#* Stores the number of command-line arguments that were passed to the shell program. Refer to the value of the total number of command line arguments passed. $1 is the first argument, $2 is the second argument and so on.

*Exit Code 1* indicates that a container shut down, either because of an application failure or because the image pointed to an invalid file. In a Unix/Linux operating system, when an application terminates with Exit Code 1, the operating system ends the process.

*Logical Operators:*
They are also known as Boolean operators. These are used to perform logical operations. 
‚Ä¢	Logical AND (&&): This is a binary operator, which returns true if both the operands are true otherwise returns false.
‚Ä¢	Logical OR (||): This is a binary operator, which returns true is either of the operand is true or both the operands are true and return false if none of them is false.
‚Ä¢	Not Equal to (!): This is a unary operator which returns true if the operand is false and returns false if the operand is true.

#!/bin/bash
echo "Enter first number: "
read one
echo "Enter second number: "
read two
echo "Enter third number: "
read three
if [ $one -gt $two ] && [ $one -gt $three ]; then
	echo "First number is largest"
elif [ $two -gt $three ]; then
	echo "Second number is largest"
else
	echo "Third number is largest"
fi

*Program*
n=$#
i=1

echo "Number of arguments:" $n

if [ $n -eq 0 ]
then

*Description:*
*Shift* is a built-in command in bash which after getting executed, shifts/move the command line arguments to one position left. "shift 1" and "shift" (with no argument) do the same thing.
*Syntax:*
	shift [n]
*Example:*
#! /bin/bash
# total number of command line arguments
echo "Total argument passed are: $#"
# to show command line arguments
echo "The arguments are: $*"
echo "First argument is: $1"
shift 2
echo "First argument after shift 2: $1"
shift
echo "First argument after shift: $1"

Shell Script to print command line arguments Type 2
*Program*
#!/bin/sh

n=$#

echo "Number of command line arguments:" $n

if [ $n -gt 0 ]
then
	echo "List of arguments"
	for arg in $@
	do
		echo "$arg"
	done
else
	echo "No arguments"
fi

*Output*

List of arguments
hello
world
how
are
you?

*Description:*
*$@* Stores all the arguments that were entered on the command line.

*for* loops iterate through a set of values until the list is exhausted.
*Syntax:*
	for <variable name> in <a list of items>
	do 
		<some command> 
	done
*Example:*
	#! /bin/bash
	clear
	for i in 1 2 3 4
	do
		echo ‚Äú$i‚Äù
	done

12/07/2022, 8:45 am - Sir Ameen Alam: What is a SHELL?

The command line interface is the primary interface to Linux/Unix operating systems.
Shells are how command-line interfaces are implemented in Linux/Unix.
Each shell has varying capabilities and features and the user should choose the shell
that best suits their needs.
The shell is simply an application running on top of the kernel and provides a powerful
interface to the system.

12/07/2022, 9:31 am - +92 333 2227262: What are the differences?

$ chmod a+rwx filename
Rwx permission to all users (user + group + others) 

$ chmod ugo+rwx filename
Assign rwx for user, group and ithers
Same as first one

$ chmod +rwx filename
Assign rwx for user on file 

$ chmod 777 filename
rwx to all users(user + group + others) on file

# chmod -R 777 dirname
rwx permissions recursively to all groups for all the files and folders inside directory
